It is called before the actual working methods {@link\n51:      * #deserialize} and thus suitable for one time setup work.\n52:      *\n53:      * <p>The provided {@link InitializationContext} can be used to access additional features such\n54:      * as e.g. registering user metrics.\n55:      *\n56:      * @param context Contextual information that can be used during initialization.\n57:      */\n58:     @PublicEvolving\n59:     default void open(InitializationContext context) throws Exception {}\n60: \n61:     /**\n62:      * Deserializes the byte message.\n63:      *\n64:      * @param message The message, as a byte array.\n65:      * @return The deserialized message as an object (null if the message cannot be deserialized).\n66:      */\n67:     T deserialize(byte[] message) throws IOException;\n68: \n69:     /**\n70:      * Deserializes the byte message.\n71:      *\n72:      * <p>Can output multiple records through the {@link Collector}. Note that number and size of\n73:      * the produced records should be relatively small. Depending on the source implementation\n74:      * records can be buffered in memory or collecting records might delay emitting checkpoint\n75:      * barrier.\n76:      *\n77:      * @param message The message, as a byte array.\n78:      * @param out The collector to put the resulting messages.\n79:      */\n80:     @PublicEvolving\n81:     default void deserialize(byte[] message, Collector<T> out) throws IOException {\n82:         T deserialize = deserialize(message);\n83:         if (deserialize != null) {\n84:             out.collect(deserialize);\n85:         }\n86:     }\n87: \n88:     /**\n89:      * Method to decide whether the element signals the end of the stream. If true is returned the\n90:      * element won't be emitted.\n91:      *\n92:      * @param nextElement The element to test for the end-of-stream signal.\n93:      * @return True, if the element signals end of stream, false otherwise.\n94:      */\n95:     boolean isEndOfStream(T nextElement);\n96: \n97:     /**\n98:      * A contextual information provided for {@link #open(InitializationContext)} method. The consumer can run in multiple parallel instances, each of which will\n171:     pull data from one or more Kafka partitions.\n172: \n173:     The Flink Kafka Consumer participates in checkpointing and guarantees that no data is lost\n174:     during a failure, and that the computation processes elements 'exactly once. Implementations convert data of type T into byte arrays using the serialize(String topic, T data) method. This is used by Kafka producers.\\n2. `org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.Deserializer<T>` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/serialization/Deserializer.java) - An interface for converting bytes to objects. Implementations deserialize byte data into objects of type T using the deserialize(String topic, byte[] data) method. This is used by Kafka consumers.\\n\\nBoth interfaces extend Closeable and provide configure(Map<String, ?> configs, boolean isKey) for initialization.\\n\\n**Flink Side (Stream Deserialization Schema):**\\n\\nIn `github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc`, Flink defines its own deserialization abstraction:\\n1. `org.apache.flink.api.common.serialization.DeserializationSchema<T>` (flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/common/serialization/DeserializationSchema.java) - Flink's abstraction for converting byte messages from data sources (such as Apache Kafka) into data types that Flink processes. The key method is deserialize(byte[] message) which returns a T object. It also implements ResultTypeQueryable<T> to describe the produced type.\\n\\n**The Bridge:**\\n\\nFlink's Kafka connector (org.apache.flink.connector.kafka.source.reader.deserializer.KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema) serves as the adapter that bridges these two interfaces. It wraps Kafka's Deserializer<T> and adapts it to work with Flink's DeserializationSchema abstraction. When Flink reads from Kafka, it uses KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema to take Kafka's ConsumerRecord and convert it using Kafka's built-in Deserializer implementations, while presenting the results as a Flink DeserializationSchema.\\n\\nKey differences:\\n- Kafka's Deserializer is topic-aware (takes topic as parameter)\\n- Flink's DeserializationSchema is more abstracted and topic-agnostic\\n- Kafka deserializers are configured via key.deserializer/value.deserializer configs\\n- Flink schemas support multiple deserialization variants through Collector pattern\\n\\nThe integration is particularly important for the Flink Kafka Connector source implementations, which must translate Kafka's byte-oriented, ConsumerRecord-based API into Flink's strongly-typed, schema-aware stream processing model.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":937,"cache_read_input_tokens":104657,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":937},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"32628b87-7e04-4db5-a32e-a6eea0fbc63a","uuid":"6662f63b-2f72-4bcd-8304-8cb42c04640c"}

This is used by Kafka producers.\\n2. `org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.Deserializer<T>` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/serialization/Deserializer.java) - An interface for converting bytes to objects. Implementations deserialize byte data into objects of type T using the deserialize(String topic, byte[] data) method. This is used by Kafka consumers.\\n\\nBoth interfaces extend Closeable and provide configure(Map<String, ?> configs, boolean isKey) for initialization.\\n\\n**Flink Side (Stream Deserialization Schema):**\\n\\nIn `github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc`, Flink defines its own deserialization abstraction:\\n1. `org.apache.flink.api.common.serialization.DeserializationSchema<T>` (flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/common/serialization/DeserializationSchema.java) - Flink's abstraction for converting byte messages from data sources (such as Apache Kafka) into data types that Flink processes. The key method is deserialize(byte[] message) which returns a T object. It also implements ResultTypeQueryable<T> to describe the produced type.\\n\\n**The Bridge:**\\n\\nFlink's Kafka connector (org.apache.flink.connector.kafka.source.reader.deserializer.KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema) serves as the adapter that bridges these two interfaces. It wraps Kafka's Deserializer<T> and adapts it to work with Flink's DeserializationSchema abstraction. When Flink reads from Kafka, it uses KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema to take Kafka's ConsumerRecord and convert it using Kafka's built-in Deserializer implementations, while presenting the results as a Flink DeserializationSchema.\\n\\nKey differences:\\n- Kafka's Deserializer is topic-aware (takes topic as parameter)\\n- Flink's DeserializationSchema is more abstracted and topic-agnostic\\n- Kafka deserializers are configured via key.deserializer/value.deserializer configs\\n- Flink schemas support multiple deserialization variants through Collector pattern\\n\\nThe integration is particularly important for the Flink Kafka Connector source implementations, which must translate Kafka's byte-oriented, ConsumerRecord-based API into Flink's strongly-typed, schema-aware stream processing model.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

(clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/serialization/Serializer.java) - An interface for converting objects to bytes. Implementations convert data of type T into byte arrays using the serialize(String topic, T data) method. This is used by Kafka producers.\\n2. `org.apache.kafka.common.serialization.Deserializer<T>` (clients/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/common/serialization/Deserializer.java) - An interface for converting bytes to objects. This is used by Kafka consumers.\\n\\nBoth interfaces extend Closeable and provide configure(Map<String, ?> configs, boolean isKey) for initialization.\\n\\n**Flink Side (Stream Deserialization Schema):**\\n\\nIn `github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc`, Flink defines its own deserialization abstraction:\\n1. `org.apache.flink.api.common.serialization.DeserializationSchema<T>` (flink-core/src/main/java/org/apache/flink/api/common/serialization/DeserializationSchema.java) - Flink's abstraction for converting byte messages from data sources (such as Apache Kafka) into data types that Flink processes. The key method is deserialize(byte[] message) which returns a T object. It also implements ResultTypeQueryable<T> to describe the produced type.\\n\\n**The Bridge:**\\n\\nFlink's Kafka connector (org.apache.flink.connector.kafka.source.reader.deserializer.KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema) serves as the adapter that bridges these two interfaces. It wraps Kafka's Deserializer<T> and adapts it to work with Flink's DeserializationSchema abstraction. When Flink reads from Kafka, it uses KafkaRecordDeserializationSchema to take Kafka's ConsumerRecord and convert it using Kafka's built-in Deserializer implementations, while presenting the results as a Flink DeserializationSchema.\\n\\nKey differences:\\n- Kafka's Deserializer is topic-aware (takes topic as parameter)\\n- Flink's DeserializationSchema is more abstracted and topic-agnostic\\n- Kafka deserializers are configured via key.deserializer/value.deserializer configs\\n- Flink schemas support multiple deserialization variants through Collector pattern\\n\\nThe integration is particularly important for the Flink Kafka Connector source implementations, which must translate Kafka's byte-oriented, ConsumerRecord-based API into Flink's strongly-typed, schema-aware stream processing model.\"\n    43→}\n    44→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
